import sqlite3
conn = sqlite3.connect('dialer.db')
cursor = conn.cursor()

print("Lead Status Distribution:")
cursor.execute('SELECT status, COUNT(*) FROM leads GROUP BY status')
for row in cursor.fetchall():
    print(f'  {row[0]}: {row[1]}')

print("\nCampaign Details:")
cursor.execute('SELECT id, name, status FROM campaigns')
for row in cursor.fetchall():
    print(f'  ID: {row[0]}, Name: {row[1]}, Status: {row[2]}')

conn.close()

import sqlite3
conn = sqlite3.connect('dialer.db')
cursor = conn.cursor()

# Reset stuck leads
cursor.execute("UPDATE leads SET status='NEW' WHERE status='CALLING'")
affected = cursor.rowcount
conn.commit()

print(f"Reset {affected} leads from CALLING to NEW")

# Show updated status
cursor.execute('SELECT status, COUNT(*) FROM leads GROUP BY status')
print("\nUpdated Lead Status Distribution:")
for row in cursor.fetchall():
    print(f'  {row[0]}: {row[1]}')

conn.close()
EOF

import sqlite3
conn = sqlite3.connect('dialer.db')
cursor = conn.cursor()

# Check leads and their campaign association
cursor.execute('SELECT id, phone_number, status, campaign_id FROM leads LIMIT 5')
print("Sample leads:")
for row in cursor.fetchall():
    print(f'  ID: {row[0]}, Phone: {row[1]}, Status: {row[2]}, Campaign ID: {row[3]}')

print(f"\nLeads for campaign 37: {cursor.fetchone()[0]}")

cursor.execute('SELECT COUNT(*) FROM leads WHERE campaign_id IS NULL')
print(f"Leads with NULL campaign_id: {cursor.fetchone()[0]}")

conn.close()

import sqlite3
from datetime import datetime

conn = sqlite3.connect('dialer.db')
cursor = conn.cursor()

# Check next_call_time for leads in campaign 37
cursor.execute('''
    SELECT id, status, next_call_time, datetime('now') as current_time
    FROM leads
    WHERE campaign_id = 37 AND status = 'NEW'
    LIMIT 5
''')

print("Sample leads for campaign 37 with NEW status:")
print("ID | Status | next_call_time | Current Time")
print("-" * 80)
for row in cursor.fetchall():
    print(f"{row[0]} | {row[1]} | {row[2]} | {row[3]}")

# Count how many have future next_call_time
cursor.execute('''
    SELECT COUNT(*)
    FROM leads
    WHERE campaign_id = 37 
    AND status = 'NEW'
    AND next_call_time > datetime('now')
''')
future_count = cursor.fetchone()[0]

cursor.execute('''
    SELECT COUNT(*)
    FROM leads
    WHERE campaign_id = 37 
    AND status = 'NEW'
    AND (next_call_time IS NULL OR next_call_time <= datetime('now'))
''')
available_count = cursor.fetchone()[0]

print(f"\nLeads with future next_call_time: {future_count}")
print(f"Leads available to call now: {available_count}")

conn.close()

import sqlite3
conn = sqlite3.connect('dialer.db')
cursor = conn.cursor()

# Reset all CALLING leads for campaign 37 back to NEW
cursor.execute("UPDATE leads SET status='NEW' WHERE status='CALLING' AND campaign_id=37")
affected = cursor.rowcount
conn.commit()

print(f"Reset {affected} leads from CALLING to NEW for campaign 37")

conn.close()

import sqlite3
conn = sqlite3.connect('dialer.db')
cursor = conn.cursor()

# Check recent call_log entries
cursor.execute('''
    SELECT id, lead_id, disposition, start_time
    FROM call_log
    ORDER BY start_time DESC
    LIMIT 10
''')

print("Recent call log entries:")
for row in cursor.fetchall():
    print(f"  ID: {row[0]}, Lead: {row[1]}, Disposition: {row[2]}, Time: {row[3]}")

cursor.execute("SELECT COUNT(*) FROM call_log WHERE start_time > datetime('now', '-5 minutes')")
recent_calls = cursor.fetchone()[0]
print(f"\nCalls in last 5 minutes: {recent_calls}")

conn.close()

import sqlite3
import time

conn = sqlite3.connect('dialer.db')
cursor = conn.cursor()

# Reset one lead to NEW
cursor.execute("UPDATE leads SET status='NEW' WHERE campaign_id=37 LIMIT 1")
conn.commit()
lead_id = cursor.lastrowid

# Immediately check status
time.sleep(0.5)

cursor.execute("SELECT id, status FROM leads WHERE campaign_id=37 AND id=?", (lead_id,))
print("Lead after reset:", cursor.fetchone())

# Wait 2 seconds
time.sleep(2)

cursor.execute("SELECT id, status FROM leads WHERE campaign_id=37 ORDER BY id DESC LIMIT 1")
print("Lead after 2 seconds:", cursor.fetchone())

conn.close()

import sqlite3

conn = sqlite3.connect('dialer.db')
cursor = conn.cursor()

# Check lead 113
cursor.execute('''
    SELECT id, status, next_call_time, datetime('now') as now
    FROM leads
    WHERE id=113
''')
print("Lead 113:")
for row in cursor.fetchall():
    print(f"  ID: {row[0]}, Status: {row[1]}, Next Call: {row[2]}, Now: {row[3]}")

# Check if it matches the query
cursor.execute('''
    SELECT COUNT(*)
    FROM leads
    WHERE campaign_id = 37
    AND status IN ('NEW', 'CALLBACK')  
    AND (next_call_time IS NULL OR next_call_time <= datetime('now'))
''')
print(f"\nLeads matching query: {cursor.fetchone()[0]}")

# Check all NEW/CALLBACK leads for campaign 37
cursor.execute('''
    SELECT id, status, next_call_time
    FROM leads
    WHERE campaign_id = 37
    AND status IN ('NEW', 'CALLBACK', 'CALLING')
    LIMIT 10
''')
print("\nAll NEW/CALLBACK/CALLING leads for campaign 37:")
for row in cursor.fetchall():
    print(f"  ID: {row[0]}, Status: {row[1]}, Next Call: {row[2]}")

conn.close()

import sqlite3

conn = sqlite3.connect('dialer.db')
cursor = conn.cursor()

# Run the exact query the orchestrator uses
query = """
    SELECT * FROM leads
    WHERE campaign_id = 37
    AND status IN ('NEW', 'CALLBACK')
    AND (next_call_time IS NULL OR next_call_time <= datetime('now'))
    ORDER BY
        CASE WHEN status = 'CALLBACK' THEN 0 ELSE 1 END,
        next_call_time ASC,
        created_at ASC
    LIMIT 5
"""

cursor.execute(query)
rows = cursor.fetchall()

print(f"Query returned {len(rows)} leads")
for row in rows:
    print(f"  ID: {row[0]}, Phone: {row[2]}, Status: {row[3]}")

# Also check what lead 116 looks like
cursor.execute("SELECT id, campaign_id, phone_number, status, next_call_time FROM leads WHERE id=116")
lead = cursor.fetchone()
print(f"\nLead 116 details:")
print(f"  ID: {lead[0]}, Campaign: {lead[1]}, Phone: {lead[2]}, Status: {lead[3]}, Next Call: {lead[4]}")

conn.close()
EOF

import requests
from requests.auth import HTTPBasicAuth

# Twilio credentials
account_sid = "AC39ed37a2d9e427ea7aeb4c27aa368110"
auth_token = "3590e08c47cfbb31093592ec84ab4af0"

# Test 1: Verify account
print("=" * 60)
print("TWILIO ACCOUNT VERIFICATION")
print("=" * 60)

response = requests.get(
    f"https://api.twilio.com/2010-04-01/Accounts/{account_sid}.json",
    auth=HTTPBasicAuth(account_sid, auth_token)
)

if response.status_code == 200:
    account = response.json()
    print(f"✅ Account Status: {account['status']}")
    print(f"   Friendly Name: {account['friendly_name']}")
    print(f"   Type: {account['type']}")
else:

    "From": "+19544668818",

    print(f"   From: {call['from']}")
    print(f"   To: {call['to']}")
else:

[DEBUG] Bash tool invoked with command: cd /home/user/Desktop/exodus-kali-deploy && cat > /tmp/explanation.txt << 'EOF'
Let me answer both your questions.

First, about chan SIP versus P J SIP. Chan SIP is the old SIP stack that Asterisk used for years. P J SIP is the new modern replacement that came out around 2014. Think of it like upgrading from Windows XP to Windows 10 - same functionality, but way better under the hood.

You were already using P J SIP for your Twilio trunk. That's what's in your p j sip dot conf file. The problem was chan SIP was ALSO loaded, and both were trying to handle SIP traffic on port 5060. They were literally fighting over the same phone calls.

By unloading chan SIP, we didn't lose any functionality - we just removed the conflict. P J SIP can do everything chan SIP did, but better. Your Twilio trunk was already configured in P J SIP, so nothing changed there. We just got rid of the interference.

Now, about the external I P address. This is NOT location-based verification. Let me explain what's actually happening.

When Asterisk makes a call, it needs to tell Twilio "send the audio here" - that's what the S D P message does. The problem was, your Asterisk is inside a Docker container with an internal I P like 172 dot 17 dot 0 dot 2. But Twilio can't send audio to that - it's a private network address.

So Asterisk needs to advertise your PUBLIC I P address - 73 dot 139 dot 162 dot 13 - so Twilio knows where to send the audio. When we set it to "auto", Asterisk was failing to detect it and sending "null" instead. Twilio saw that and said "403 Forbidden" because it literally had nowhere to send the audio.

Now here's the important part about mobility: When you move to a different location with a different I P address, YES, you'll need to update this. But it's easy. You just change one line in the config to your new public I P, reload P J SIP, and you're good.

There are three ways to handle this: One, use "external underscore media underscore address equals auto" and hope Asterisk detects it correctly. Two, manually set it like we did now. Or three, use a dynamic DNS service or V P N so your I P never changes.

For a production system, I'd recommend either setting up a static I P from your ISP, or running this on a cloud server that has a fixed I P address. That way you never have to worry about it changing.

But to be clear: This is about AUDIO routing, not authentication. Twilio already knows who you are from your auth token. This is just telling Twilio's servers where to send the voice data. Does that make sense?
EOF

[DEBUG] Bash tool invoked with command: cat > /tmp/port_forward_explanation.txt << 'EOF'
Yes, you're exactly right to ask about port forwarding. This is actually a critical point.

Here's what's happening with the ports. For outbound calls, which is what your dialer does, you need TWO types of ports forwarded:

First, port 5060 UDP. This is for SIP signaling. The good news is, I can see your Docker container already has this mapped. Port 5060 on your host machine forwards to port 5060 in the Asterisk container. So that part is handled.

Second, and this is the important one: R T P audio ports. These are typically UDP ports in the range of 10,000 to 20,000. This is where the actual voice audio flows.

Now, here's why your calls might still work even though we haven't explicitly forwarded R T P ports: You're making OUTBOUND calls, not inbound. When you dial out, your Asterisk initiates the connection. Your router's NAT will automatically allow the RETURN traffic from Twilio because it's part of an established connection. It's like when you browse a website - you don't need to port forward because YOU started the connection.

Plus, we have "R T P symmetric" set to "yes" in your P J SIP config. This tells Asterisk to send audio back to whatever address Twilio sends audio FROM. This helps traverse NAT without explicit port forwarding.

However, for a production system, especially if you want to receive INBOUND calls, you would need to properly forward the R T P port range. Let me check what range your Asterisk is configured to use, and we can set up proper port forwarding if needed.

The short answer is: For outbound calling with your dialer, it should work without additional port forwarding because of NAT traversal and R T P symmetric mode. But for inbound calls or better reliability, yes, you'd want proper port forwarding set up.
EOF

[DEBUG] Bash tool invoked with command: edge-tts --voice "en-US-GuyNeural" --text "Alright man, here's where we're at. I found the root cause of why calls aren't working. The Asterisk AMI connection has a critical bug - the Read and Write counters are hitting max integer value instantly, like within 20 seconds of connecting. This makes it impossible for the dialer to send Originate commands to Asterisk.

What's happening is: the lead gets inserted as NEW, the dialer tries to tell Asterisk to make the call via AMI, but the AMI command fails silently because of the integer overflow. The system still increments the attempts counter though. After 3 failed attempts, there's a database trigger that automatically marks the lead as COMPLETED.

So the lead goes NEW to COMPLETED in seconds without any actual call being made. No ringing, no connection to Twilio, nothing.

I've restarted Asterisk twice now, and both times the AMI counters overflow almost immediately. This isn't normal - it should take days or weeks to hit 2 billion operations, not 20 seconds. Something is fundamentally broken, either in Asterisk itself, the AMI protocol implementation, or possibly how the SimpleAMI library is displaying these counters.

We're currently stuck in a loop where every test lead gets auto-completed without calls." --write-media /tmp/exodus_status_update.mp3 2>&1 | grep -v "^$"

I found the root cause of why calls aren't working. The Asterisk AMI connection has a critical bug - the Read and Write counters are hitting max integer value instantly, like within 20 seconds of connecting. This makes it impossible for the dialer to send Originate commands to Asterisk.

What's happening is: the lead gets inserted as NEW, the dialer tries to tell Asterisk to make the call via AMI, but the AMI command fails silently because of the integer overflow. The system still increments the attempts counter though. After 3 failed attempts, there's a database trigger that automatically marks the lead as COMPLETED.

So the lead goes NEW to COMPLETED in seconds without any actual call being made. No ringing, no connection to Twilio, nothing.

I've restarted Asterisk twice now, and both times the AMI counters overflow almost immediately. This isn't normal - it should take days or weeks to hit 2 billion operations, not 20 seconds. Something is fundamentally broken, either in Asterisk itself, the AMI protocol implementation, or possibly how the SimpleAMI library is displaying these counters.

We're currently stuck in a loop where every test lead gets auto-completed without calls." --write-media /tmp/exodus_status_update.mp3 2>&1

1. Updated P J SIP config to use the correct trunk: exodus dash dialer dot P S T N dot twilio dot com
2. Added your current IP, 73 dot 139 dot 162 dot 13, to the trunk's IP whitelist
3. Removed credential authentication from the trunk so it only uses IP-based auth
4. Updated the caller ID to match your EXODUS underscore Dialer phone number

================================================================================
## Phase 11: Twilio SIP Trunk Troubleshooting & Outbound Calling Fix (2025-11-02)
================================================================================

### Overview
Fixed critical Twilio SIP trunk authentication issues preventing outbound calls. After extensive debugging, identified and resolved multiple configuration problems that were causing 403 Forbidden errors.

### Initial Problem
- Leads going from NEW → COMPLETED without any actual calls being placed
- Dialer showing "OriginateResponse: Failure, Reason=0" 
- No audio, no ringing, calls failing silently
- Asterisk processing 0 calls

### Root Cause Discovery Process

**False Lead #1: AMI Integer Overflow (DEBUNKED)**
- Initially suspected AMI Read/Write counters showing 2,147,483,647 (max int32)
- Research revealed these are **permission bitmasks**, NOT counters
- This is completely normal for an admin user with full permissions
- AMI was working perfectly - this was a red herring

**False Lead #2: Missing Dialplan Context**
- Added audiosocket-dial context from asterisk-dialer-config.conf
- Extensions 9092-9111 for bot connections were already present
- This was already configured correctly

**False Lead #3: Module Conflict**
- Unloaded conflicting chan_sip module (was running alongside PJSIP)
- Still getting 403 Forbidden from Twilio

**Root Cause #1: NULL IP in SDP**
- PJSIP logs showed: `c=IN IP4 (null)` in SDP messages
- `external_media_address=auto` was failing to detect public IP
- **Fix**: Set explicit `external_media_address=73.139.162.13`
- Twilio needs valid IP in SDP to know where to send RTP audio

**Root Cause #2: Wrong SIP Domain**
- pjsip.conf was configured for `javierg720.sip.us1.twilio.com`
- This domain doesn't exist in the Twilio account
- User has `vicibox1.sip.twilio.com` (SIP Domain) but phone numbers are on **SIP Trunks**, not domains

**Root Cause #3: Wrong Trunk Configuration**
- Phone numbers assigned to SIP Trunks (exodus, MyDialer, EXODUS_Dialer)
- Number `+1 561 532 4683` is on **EXODUS_Dialer** trunk
- Domain should be `exodus-dialer.pstn.twilio.com`, not `vicibox1.sip.twilio.com`
- **Fix**: Updated pjsip.conf to use correct trunk domain

**Root Cause #4: IP Not in ACL**
- EXODUS_Dialer trunk ACL only had `73.138.30.222` (old server IP)
- Current IP is `73.139.162.13`
- Twilio returning 403 Forbidden due to IP mismatch
- **Fix**: Added `73.139.162.13` to trunk's IP Access Control List

**Root Cause #5: Credential Authentication Conflict**
- Trunk configured for BOTH IP ACL AND credentials
- Twilio sending 407 Proxy Authentication Required
- pjsip.conf had username="exodus-dialer" but no password match in Twilio
- **Fix**: Removed credential list from trunk, using IP-only authentication

### Final Configuration

**pjsip.conf Changes:**
```conf
[transport-udp]
type=transport
protocol=udp
bind=0.0.0.0:5060
external_media_address=73.139.162.13        # Was: auto (failed)
external_signaling_address=73.139.162.13    # Was: auto (failed)

[twilio]
type=endpoint
from_user=15615324683                        # Was: 19544668818 (wrong number)
from_domain=exodus-dialer.pstn.twilio.com    # Was: javierg720.sip.us1.twilio.com (doesn't exist)
outbound_auth=twilio
contact=sip:exodus-dialer.pstn.twilio.com    # Was: javierg720.sip.us1.twilio.com

[twilio]
type=auth
username=exodus-dialer                       # Was: javierg720
password=3590e08c47cfbb31093592ec84ab4af0
```

**Twilio Trunk Configuration (via API):**
- Trunk: EXODUS_Dialer (TK087fe28b7b9b187d7d170358d3007bb6)
- Domain: exodus-dialer.pstn.twilio.com
- Authentication: IP ACL only (removed credentials)
- ACL: Asterisk Server (AL6c4790f16a34e1c55eb2d34beeab41e4)
  - 73.138.30.222 (old server - already there)
  - **73.139.162.13 (Exodus Kali Server - ADDED)**
- Phone Number: +1 561 532 4683

### Code Changes

**dialer_orchestrator.py (lines 754-756):**
Added missing lead status update after call completion:
```python
# Update lead status after call completes
await self.db.update_lead_after_call(call_attempt.lead_id, call_status)
logger.debug(f"✅ Updated lead {call_attempt.lead_id} to status: {call_status}")
```

**Problem**: The `_handle_hangup` function was logging calls but never updating lead status, causing leads to stay stuck in CALLING.

   - Removed credential list CL4394c75e2b1521ff1d5cb77c7d1bbdae from trunk

### Critical Discoveries

1. **SIP Domains vs SIP Trunks**:
   - SIP Domains (e.g., vicibox1.sip.twilio.com) are for **registered devices** (SIP phones)
   - SIP Trunks (e.g., exodus-dialer.pstn.twilio.com) are for **outbound calling** with assigned phone numbers
   - Phone numbers can only be assigned to trunks, not domains

2. **AMI Permission Display**:
   - Read/Write values of 2,147,483,647 are **normal**
   - These are permission bitmasks showing all permissions granted
   - NOT operation counters that overflow

3. **Twilio Authentication Methods**:
   - Can use: IP ACL, Credentials, or BOTH
   - If BOTH configured, Twilio enforces BOTH
   - Simplest: IP ACL only (fewer moving parts)

4. **External IP Configuration**:
   - Required for Docker containers with private IPs
   - Twilio needs to know public IP for RTP audio routing
   - `auto` detection fails in Docker environments
   - **Must manually update if IP changes** (not portable)

5. **Port Forwarding**:
   - Port 5060 UDP (SIP signaling): Already forwarded by Docker
   - Ports 10000-10100 UDP (RTP audio): NOT forwarded
   - **Works anyway** for outbound calls due to:
     - NAT allows return traffic on initiated connections
     - `rtp_symmetric=yes` in PJSIP config
   - Would need forwarding for **inbound** calls

### Debugging Methodology

**Key Lesson: Deep research instead of guessing**
- User insisted: "Don't just try to guess it. Remember."
- Used WebSearch extensively to understand:
  - Asterisk AMI architecture (manager.c source code)
  - Twilio SIP trunk authentication methods
  - OriginateResponse reason codes
  - SIP protocol details (407, 403 responses)
- Checked actual Twilio configuration via API
- Enabled PJSIP logging to see exact SIP traffic

**Tools Used:**
- `docker exec ava-asterisk asterisk -rx "pjsip set logger on"` - SIP traffic inspection
- `docker logs ava-asterisk` - Detailed SIP INVITE/response analysis
- Twilio API - Verified trunk configuration, ACLs, phone numbers
- `curl` - Modified Twilio trunk settings programmatically

### Lessons for Future Development

1. **Always verify Twilio config via API** - Console can be misleading
2. **Test with PJSIP logging enabled** - Seeing actual SIP traffic is invaluable
3. **SIP Domains ≠ SIP Trunks** - Fundamentally different use cases
4. **External IP must be explicit in Docker** - Auto-detection fails
5. **IP ACL is simpler than credentials** - Fewer points of failure
6. **Phone number must match trunk assignment** - Check in Twilio console
7. **Manual originate tests isolate Asterisk issues** - Bypass dialer complexity
8. **User communication is critical** - Voice updates helped significantly

### Documentation References

**Twilio API Endpoints Used:**
- GET /2010-04-01/Accounts/{AccountSid}/SIP/Domains.json
- GET /v1/Trunks
- GET /v1/Trunks/{TrunkSid}/IpAccessControlLists
- POST /IpAccessControlLists/{ListSid}/IpAddresses.json
- DELETE /v1/Trunks/{TrunkSid}/CredentialLists/{ListSid}

**Asterisk CLI Commands:**
- `pjsip show endpoints` - View configured endpoints
- `pjsip show transports` - View transport configuration
- `pjsip set logger on/off` - Enable/disable SIP traffic logging
- `manager show connected` - View AMI connections
- `core show channels` - View active calls
- `dialplan show audiosocket-dial` - Verify dialplan loaded

**Database Schema:**
- Trigger: `auto_complete_lead_on_max_attempts` - Auto-completes at max_attempts
- Default: `max_attempts=3` - Leads auto-complete after 3 failed calls
- Status flow: NEW → CALLING → (should go to COMPLETED/NO_ANSWER/BUSY/etc)
